MARGIN-TOP:26px" align=center>F-6</p> <p style=MARGIN:0px><br></p> <hr size=1 noshade style="MARGIN-BOTTOM:9px; PADDING-TOP:9px"> <p style="MARGIN-BOTTOM:6px; PAGE-BREAK-BEFORE:always; MARGIN-TOP:0px" align=center><b>ADVANSOURCE BIOMATERIALS CORPORATION</b></p> <p style="MARGIN-BOTTOM:6px; MARGIN-TOP:0px" align=center><b>NOTES TO CONSOLIDATED FINANCIAL STATEMENTS</b></p> <p style=MARGIN:0px><br></p> <p style="MARGIN-BOTTOM:-2px; FLOAT:left; MARGIN-TOP:0px; WIDTH:48px; TEXT-INDENT:24px"><b>A.</b></p> <p style="MARGIN-BOTTOM:6px; PADDING-LEFT:48px; MARGIN-TOP:0px; TEXT-INDENT:-2px" align=justify><b>Nature of Business</b></p> <p style="MARGIN-BOTTOM:6px; CLEAR:left; MARGIN-TOP:6px; TEXT-INDENT:24px">AdvanSource Biomaterials Corporation (&#147;AdvanSource&#148; or the &#147;Company&#148;) develops advanced polymer materials which provide critical characteristics in the design and development of medical devices. &nbsp;The Company&#146;s biomaterials are used in devices that are designed for treating a broad range of anatomical sites and disease states. &nbsp;The Company&#146;s business model leverages its proprietary materials science technology and manufacturing expertise in order to expand product sales and royalty and license fee income.</p> <p style="MARGIN-BOTTOM:6px; MARGIN-TOP:6px; TEXT-INDENT:24px">The Company<font style="FONT-FAMILY:Arial Unicode MS,Times New Roman">&#146;</font>s technology, notably products such as ChronoFlex&#174;, HydroMed<font style="FONT-FAMILY:Arial Unicode MS,Times New Roman">&#153;</font>, and HydroThane<font style="FONT-FAMILY:Arial Unicode MS,Times New Roman">&#153;</font>, which have been developed to overcome a wide range of design and functional challenges such as the need for dimensional stability, ease of manufacture and demanding physical properties to overcoming environmental stress cracking and providing heightened lubricity for ease of insertion. &nbsp;The Company&#146;s new product extensions customize proprietary polymers for specific customer applications in a wide range of device categories.</p> <p style="MARGIN-BOTTOM:6px; MARGIN-TOP:6px; TEXT-INDENT:24px" align=justify>The Company&#146;s corporate, development and manufacturing operations are located in Wilmington, Massachusetts.</p> <p style="MARGIN-BOTTOM:6px; MARGIN-TOP:6px" align=justify><i>Fiscal Year</i></p> <p style="MARGIN-BOTTOM:6px; MARGIN-TOP:6px; TEXT-INDENT:24px" align=justify>The Company&#146;s fiscal year ends on March 31. &nbsp;References herein to fiscal 2013 and/or fiscal 2012 refer to the fiscal years ended March 31, 2013 and/or 2012, respectively.</p> <p style="MARGIN-BOTTOM:-2px; FLOAT:left; MARGIN-TOP:0px; WIDTH:48px; TEXT-INDENT:24px"><b>B.</b></p> <p style="MARGIN-BOTTOM:6px; PADDING-LEFT:48px; MARGIN-TOP:0px; TEXT-INDENT:-2px" align=justify><b>Summary of Significant Accounting Policies</b></p> <p style="MARGIN-BOTTOM:6px; CLEAR:left; MARGIN-TOP:0px; TEXT-INDENT:24px" align=justify><i>Accounting Principles</i></p> <p style="MARGIN-BOTTOM:6px; MARGIN-TOP:0px; TEXT-INDENT:24px" align=justify>The consolidated financial statements and accompanying notes are prepared in accordance with U.S. generally accepted accounting principles (&#147;GAAP&#148;).</p> <p style="MARGIN-BOTTOM:6px; MARGIN-TOP:0px; TEXT-INDENT:24px" align=justify><i>Basis of Consolidation</i></p> <p style="MARGIN-BOTTOM:6px; MARGIN-TOP:0px; TEXT-INDENT:24px" align=justify>The consolidated financial statements include the accounts of the Company and its wholly-owned subsidiary, CardioTech Realty, LLC. &nbsp;CardioTech Realty, LLC, which has no operating activities and was formed for purposes of holding title to the Company&#146;s property located in Wilmington, Massachusetts, was involuntarily dissolved by the Commonwealth of Massachusetts on April 30, 2009. &nbsp;On June 24, 2011, CardioTech Realty, LLC was reinstated as a corporation in good standing by the Commonwealth of Massachusetts. &nbsp;On December 22, 2011, the Company sold its land and building (Notes F and I).</p> <p style="MARGIN-BOTTOM:6px; MARGIN-TOP:0px; TEXT-INDENT:24px" align=justify><i>Use of Accounting Estimates</i></p> <p style="MARGIN-BOTTOM:6px; MARGIN-TOP:0px; TEXT-INDENT:24px" align=justify>The preparation of financial statements in conformity with U.S. GAAP requires management to make certain estimates and assumptions that affect the reported amounts of assets and liabilities and disclosure of contingent assets and liabilities at the date of the consolidated financial statements and the reported amounts of revenue and expenses during the reporting period. &nbsp;Actual results could differ from those estimates.<a name=A_SummaryOfSignificantAccountingP_023349></p> <p style="MARGIN-BOTTOM:6px; PADDING-LEFT:24px; MARGIN-TOP:6px" align=justify><i>Cash</i></p> <p style="MARGIN-BOTTOM:6px; MARGIN-TOP:6px; TEXT-INDENT:24px" align=justify>Cash includes cash on hand, is deposited at one area bank and may exceed federally insured limits at times.</p> <p style=MARGIN:6px align=justify><br><br></p> <p style="MARGIN-BOTTOM:0px; MARGIN-TOP:26px" align=center>F-7</p> <p style=MARGIN:0px><br></p> <hr size=1 noshade style="MARGIN-BOTTOM:9px; PADDING-TOP:9px"> <p style="MARGIN-BOTTOM:6px; PAGE-BREAK-BEFORE:always; MARGIN-TOP:0px" align=center><b>ADVANSOURCE BIOMATERIALS CORPORATION</b></p> <p style="MARGIN-BOTTOM:6px; MARGIN-TOP:0px" align=center><b>NOTES TO CONSOLIDATED FINANCIAL STATEMENTS</b></p> <p style=MARGIN:0px><br></p> <p style="MARGIN-BOTTOM:6px; PADDING-LEFT:24px; MARGIN-TOP:6px" align=justify><i>Revenue Recognition</i></p> <p style="MARGIN-BOTTOM:6px; MARGIN-TOP:0px; TEXT-INDENT:24px" align=justify>The Company generates revenue primarily from (i) the sale of polymer products and (ii) license, royalty and development agreements.</p> <p style="MARGIN-BOTTOM:6px; MARGIN-TOP:0px; TEXT-INDENT:48px" align=justify><u>Product Sales</u></p> <p style="MARGIN-BOTTOM:6px; PADDING-LEFT:24px; MARGIN-TOP:0px; TEXT-INDENT:24px" align=justify>Revenues generated from the sale of polymer products is recognized upon shipment, provided that a purchase order has been received or a contract has been executed, there are no uncertainties regarding customer acceptance, the sales price is fixed or determinable and collection is deemed reasonably assured. &nbsp;If uncertainties regarding customer acceptance exist, the Company recognizes revenues when those uncertainties are resolved and title has been transferred to the customer. &nbsp;Amounts collected or billed prior to satisfying the above revenue recognition criteria are recorded as deferred revenue.</p> <p style="MARGIN-BOTTOM:6px; MARGIN-TOP:0px; TEXT-INDENT:48px" align=justify><u>License, Royalty and Development Fees</u></p> <p style="MARGIN-BOTTOM:6px; PADDING-LEFT:24px; MARGIN-TOP:0px; TEXT-INDENT:24px" align=justify>The Company also receives license, royalty and development fees, pursuant to agreements with its customers, for the use of its proprietary polymer biomaterials. &nbsp;The terms of the various license, royalty and development agreements may contain multiple deliverables which may include (i) licenses to use the Company&#146;s polymer biomaterials in the customer&#146;s end-product medical device, (ii) research and development activities, (iii) services and/or (iv) the manufacturing of polymer biomaterials. &nbsp;Payments to the Company under these agreements may include non-refundable license fees, payments for research and development activities, payments for the manufacture of polymer materials, payments based upon the achievement of certain milestones, payments for the use of the Company&#146;s polymer biomaterials in the customer&#146;s end-product, and/or royalties earned on the sale of the customer&#146;s end-product.</p> <p style="MARGIN-BOTTOM:6px; PADDING-LEFT:24px; MARGIN-TOP:0px; TEXT-INDENT:24px" align=justify>In October 2009, the FASB issued Accounting Standards Update (&#147;ASU&#148;) 2009-13, <i>&#147;Multiple-Deliverable Revenue Arrangements (&#147;ASU 2009-13&#148;).&#148;</i> &nbsp;The Company adopted the provisions of the new multiple-element arrangement guidance summarized in ASU 2009-13 on April 1, 2011 on a prospective basis. &nbsp;Therefore, this guidance is applicable to any contract entered into or modified on or subsequent to the date of adoption. &nbsp;This guidance establishes a new hierarchy for determining the amount of arrangement consideration to allocate to each separable deliverable in an arrangement. &nbsp;For those deliverables that qualify as separate units of accounting, the Company must assign value based on each deliverable&#146;s &nbsp;vendor-specific objective evidence (&#147;VSOE&#148;) of fair value if available, third-party evidence (&#147;TPE&#148;) of its value if VSOE is not available, or estimated selling price (&#147;ESP&#148;) if neither VSOE or TPE is available. &nbsp;Arrangement consideration is then allocated to all deliverables using the relative selling price method. &nbsp;The residual method of allocation is not permissible under the new guidance.</p> <p style="MARGIN-BOTTOM:6px; PADDING-LEFT:24px; MARGIN-TOP:0px; TEXT-INDENT:24px" align=justify>In determining the separate units of accounting, management evaluates whether the delivered element has standalone value to the customer based on the consideration of the relevant facts and circumstances for each arrangement. &nbsp;Factors considered in this determination include the customer&#146;s research, development, production and product commercialization capabilities and the availability of these capabilities, as well as polymer development and manufacture expertise in the general marketplace. &nbsp;In addition, the Company considers whether the customer can use the license for its intended purpose without the receipt of the remaining deliverables, whether the value of the license is dependent on the undelivered items and whether there are other vendors that can provide the undelivered item.</p> <p style="MARGIN-BOTTOM:6px; MARGIN-TOP:0px" align=justify><br><br></p> <p style="MARGIN-BOTTOM:0px; MARGIN-TOP:26px" align=center>F-8</p> <p style=MARGIN:0px><br></p> <hr size=1 noshade style="MARGIN-BOTTOM:9px; PADDING-TOP:9px"> <p style="MARGIN-BOTTOM:6px; PAGE-BREAK-BEFORE:always; MARGIN-TOP:0px" align=center><b>ADVANSOURCE BIOMATERIALS CORPORATION</b></p> <p style="MARGIN-BOTTOM:6px; MARGIN-TOP:0px" align=center><b>NOTES TO CONSOLIDATED FINANCIAL STATEMENTS</b></p> <p style=MARGIN:0px><br></p> <p style="MARGIN-BOTTOM:6px; PADDING-LEFT:24px; MARGIN-TOP:0px; TEXT-INDENT:24px" align=justify>Management performs extensive analysis to determine the value, or selling price, of each unit of accounting. &nbsp;The Company has been unable to establish VSOE due to the fact that it does not typically enter into arrangements where technology is licensed separately, rather, its arrangements are commingled with fees from royalties, usage of polymers within customer end-products, minimum purchases of polymer products manufactured and sold to customers by the Company, or a combination of the aforementioned. &nbsp;Additionally, the Company has been unable to obtain TPE for any of its deliverables, without undue cost and effort. &nbsp;Generally, the Company&#146;s go-to-market strategy differs from that of its peers and its offerings contain a significant level of customization and differentiation such that the Company&#146;s services are not interchangeable with those of its competitors. &nbsp;Furthermore, the Company is unable to reliably determine what similar competitor products&#146; selling prices are on a standalone basis.</p> <p style="MARGIN-BOTTOM:6px; PADDING-LEFT:24px; MARGIN-TOP:0px; TEXT-INDENT:24px" align=justify>Management&#146;s ESP is used for the Company&#146;s licensing, royalty and development arrangements. &nbsp;The Company determines that ESP for the elements of these arrangements is based on several factors, including, but not limited to, the terms of the arrangements, market conditions, historical analysis of contracts having similar elements, and the Company&#146;s internal costs and gross margin objectives. &nbsp;The determination of ESP is made through consultation with and formal approval by the Company&#146;s management. &nbsp;ESP for certain consultative services is determined based on consideration of time incurred by the Company to perform these services, consulting fees charged on a per-hour basis by the Company and by its vendors, and the Company&#146;s pricing methodologies.</p> <p style="MARGIN-BOTTOM:6px; PADDING-LEFT:24px; MARGIN-TOP:0px; TEXT-INDENT:24px" align=justify>The Company&#146;s arrangements generally do not include any provisions for cancellation, termination, or refunds that would significantly impact recognized revenue.</p> <p style="MARGIN-BOTTOM:6px; PADDING-LEFT:24px; MARGIN-TOP:0px; TEXT-INDENT:24px" align=justify>In June 2011, the Company entered into a non-exclusive license agreement and a consulting services agreement (collectively, the &#147;Agreements&#148;) with a major international developer and manufacturer of medical devices (&#147;Customer&#148;), which generally provides the Customer the right to use and know-how to produce a specific proprietary polymer biomaterial for a specific field of use (the &#147;Licensed Polymer&#148;) within the Customer&#146;s suite of medical device products. &nbsp;In accordance with the applicable accounting guidance, the Company determined the Agreements included the following units of accounting: &nbsp;(i) transfer of technology and know-how related to the Licensed Polymer, (ii) consulting services related to the establishment of a facility to manufacture the Licensed Polymer by the Customer, (iii) assisting the Customer in validating the Licensed Polymer produced by the Customer, and (iv) consulting with the Customer in connection with the Customer&#146;s efforts to obtain various regulatory approvals for medical devices incorporating the Licensed Polymer.</p> <p style="MARGIN-BOTTOM:6px; PADDING-LEFT:24px; MARGIN-TOP:0px; TEXT-INDENT:24px" align=justify>Upon the execution of the Agreements, the Company received an up-front payment of $150,000, and in July 2011, the Company received an additional $250,000 upon the transfer of technology and know-how related to the Licensed Polymer. &nbsp;The Agreements also provide for additional payments upon the achievement of certain milestones, as previously described, each of which the Company considers substantive, and could total up to an additional $1,100,000. &nbsp;The Agreements do not provide for any royalties or other fees upon the achievement of any or all of the milestones. &nbsp;The Company determined that the transfer of technology and know-how of the Licensed Polymer represented a separate unit of accounting, and upon delivery, in accordance with the applicable accounting guidance, the Company recognized $400,000 of revenue during the fiscal year ended March 31, 2012. &nbsp;During fiscal 2013, the Company achieved an additional milestone in connection with the functional installation of certain production equipment and recognized $20,000 of revenue during the fiscal year ended March 31, 2013.</p> <p style="MARGIN-BOTTOM:6px; PADDING-LEFT:24px; MARGIN-TOP:6px; TEXT-INDENT:24px" align=justify>The adoption of this guidance resulted in an increase to revenue during the fiscal years ended March 31, 2013 and 2012 of $20,000 and $400,000, respectively, over the amount which would have been recognized under the principles used during the fiscal year ended March 31, 2011. &nbsp;Prior to the adoption of this guidance, the Company would have been required to defer revenue for license, royalty or development agreements until completion of the contracts or until recognized utilizing a proportional performance method of revenue recognition, based on the terms of the various agreements.</p> <p style=MARGIN:6px align=justify><br><br></p> <p style="MARGIN-BOTTOM:0px; MARGIN-TOP:26px" align=center>F-9</p> <p style=MARGIN:0px><br></p> <hr size=1 noshade style="MARGIN-BOTTOM:9px; PADDING-TOP:9px"> <p style="MARGIN-BOTTOM:6px; PAGE-BREAK-BEFORE:always; MARGIN-TOP:0px" align=center><b>ADVANSOURCE BIOMATERIALS CORPORATION</b></p> <p style="MARGIN-BOTTOM:6px; MARGIN-TOP:0px" align=center><b>NOTES TO CONSOLIDATED FINANCIAL STATEMENTS</b></p> <p style=MARGIN:0px><br></p> <p style="MARGIN-BOTTOM:6px; PADDING-LEFT:24px; MARGIN-TOP:6px" align=justify><i>Research, Development and Regulatory Expense</i></p> <p style="MARGIN-BOTTOM:6px; MARGIN-TOP:6px; TEXT-INDENT:24px" align=justify>Research, development and regulatory expenditures for the years ended March 31, 2013 and 2012 were $444,000 and $605,000, respectively, and consisted primarily of salaries and related costs and are expensed as incurred. &nbsp;The Company has two full time research and development employees that work on a variety of projects, including production support.</p> <p style="MARGIN-BOTTOM:6px; MARGIN-TOP:6px; TEXT-INDENT:24px" align=justify><i>Advertising Costs</i></p> <p style="MARGIN-BOTTOM:6px; MARGIN-TOP:6px; TEXT-INDENT:24px" align=justify>Advertising costs are expensed as incurred or at the first time the advertising takes place. &nbsp;Advertising costs for the years ended March 31, 2013 and 2012 were $15,000 and $4,000, respectively.</p> <p style="MARGIN-BOTTOM:6px; MARGIN-TOP:6px; TEXT-INDENT:24px" align=justify><i>Reporting Comprehensive Loss</i></p> <p style="MARGIN-BOTTOM:6px; MARGIN-TOP:6px; TEXT-INDENT:24px" align=justify>Comprehensive income (loss) is the total of net income (loss) and all other non-owner changes in equity including such items as unrealized holding gains (losses) on securities classified as available-for-sale and foreign currency translation adjustments. &nbsp;For the years ended March 31, 2013 and 2012, comprehensive loss is equal to net loss.</p> <p style="MARGIN-BOTTOM:6px; PADDING-LEFT:24px; MARGIN-TOP:6px" align=justify><i>Basic and Diluted Earnings(Loss) Per Share</i></p> <p style="MARGIN-BOTTOM:6px; MARGIN-TOP:6px; TEXT-INDENT:24px" align=justify>Basic earnings (loss) per share is computed by dividing net income (loss) by the weighted-average number of common shares outstanding during the period. &nbsp;Diluted earnings (loss) per share are based upon the weighted-average number of common shares outstanding during the period plus additional weighted-average common equivalent shares outstanding during the period. &nbsp;Common equivalent shares result from the assumed exercise of outstanding stock options and warrants, the proceeds of which are then assumed to have been used to repurchase outstanding common stock using the treasury stock method. &nbsp;In addition, the numerator is adjusted for any changes in income or loss that would result from the assumed conversion of potential shares. &nbsp;At March 31, 2013 and 2012, potentially dilutive shares of 2,063,798 and 2,349,417, respectively, were excluded from the loss per share calculations because their effect would be antidilutive. &nbsp;Shares deemed to be antidilutive include stock options and warrants.</p> <p style="MARGIN-BOTTOM:6px; MARGIN-TOP:6px; TEXT-INDENT:24px" align=justify><i>Accounts Receivable</i></p> <p style="MARGIN-BOTTOM:6px; MARGIN-TOP:6px; TEXT-INDENT:24px" align=justify>The Company performs various analyses to evaluate accounts receivable balances and record an allowance for bad debts based on the estimated collectability of the accounts such that the amounts reflect estimated net realizable value. &nbsp;Account balances are charged off against the allowance after significant collection efforts have been made and potential for recovery is not considered probable. &nbsp;As of March 31, 2013 and 2012, the Company&#146;s allowance for doubtful accounts was $5,000.</p> <p style="MARGIN-BOTTOM:6px; MARGIN-TOP:6px; TEXT-INDENT:24px" align=justify><i>Inventories</i></p> <p style="MARGIN-BOTTOM:6px; MARGIN-TOP:6px; TEXT-INDENT:24px" align=justify>The Company values its inventory at the lower of our actual cost or the current estimated market value. &nbsp;The Company regularly reviews inventory quantities on hand and inventory commitments with suppliers and records a provision for excess and obsolete inventory based primarily on our historical usage for the prior twelve-month period. &nbsp;Although the Company makes every effort to ensure the accuracy of our forecasts of future product demand, any significant unanticipated change in demand or technological developments could have a significant impact on the value of the Company&#146;s inventory and its reported operating results. &nbsp;As of March 31, 2013 and 2012, the Company&#146;s allowance for obsolete and excess inventory was $166,000 and $133,000, respectively.</p> <p style=MARGIN:6px align=justify><br><br></p> <p style="MARGIN-BOTTOM:0px; MARGIN-TOP:26px" align=center>F-10</p> <p style=MARGIN:0px><br></p> <hr size=1 noshade style="MARGIN-BOTTOM:9px; PADDING-TOP:9px"> <p style="MARGIN-BOTTOM:6px; PAGE-BREAK-BEFORE:always; MARGIN-TOP:0px" align=center><b>ADVANSOURCE BIOMATERIALS CORPORATION</b></p> <p style="MARGIN-BOTTOM:6px; MARGIN-TOP:0px" align=center><b>NOTES TO CONSOLIDATED FINANCIAL STATEMENTS</b></p> <p style=MARGIN:0px><br></p> <p style="MARGIN-BOTTOM:6px; PADDING-LEFT:24px; MARGIN-TOP:6px" align=justify><i>Property and Equipment</i></p> <p style="MARGIN-BOTTOM:6px; MARGIN-TOP:6px; TEXT-INDENT:24px" align=justify>Property and equipment are stated at cost. &nbsp;Equipment is depreciated using the straight-line method over the estimated useful lives of the assets, ranging from three to seven years. &nbsp;Building improvements are amortized using the straight-line method over the remaining estimated life of the building at the time the improvement is put into service. &nbsp;The Company&#146;s building is depreciated using the straight-line method over 40 years. &nbsp;Land is not depreciated. &nbsp;Expenditures for repairs and maintenance are charged to expense as incurred. &nbsp;The Company records construction in process in the appropriate asset category and commences depreciation upon completion and commencement of use of the asset.</p> <p style="MARGIN-BOTTOM:6px; MARGIN-TOP:6px; TEXT-INDENT:24px" align=justify><i>Deferred Financing Costs</i></p> <p style="MARGIN-BOTTOM:6px; MARGIN-TOP:6px; TEXT-INDENT:24px" align=justify>The Company has capitalized certain costs related to the issuance of debt. &nbsp;These costs are amortized to interest expense on a straight-line basis over the term of the debt. During the fiscal years ended March 31, 2103 and 2012, amortization expense related to deferred financing costs were $7,000 and $18,000, respectively.</p> <p style="MARGIN-BOTTOM:6px; PADDING-LEFT:24px; MARGIN-TOP:6px" align=justify><i>Income Taxes</i></p> <p style="MARGIN-BOTTOM:6px; MARGIN-TOP:6px; TEXT-INDENT:24px" align=justify>The provision for income taxes includes federal, state, local and foreign taxes. Income taxes are accounted for under the liability method. &nbsp;Deferred tax assets and liabilities are recognized for the estimated future tax consequences of temporary differences between the financial statement carrying amounts and their respective tax bases. &nbsp;Deferred tax assets and liabilities are measured using enacted tax rates expected to apply to taxable income in the year in which the temporary differences are expected to be recovered or settled. &nbsp;The Company evaluates the realizability of its deferred tax assets and establishes a valuation allowance when it is more likely than not that all or a portion of deferred tax assets will not be realized.</p> <p style="MARGIN-BOTTOM:6px; MARGIN-TOP:6px; TEXT-INDENT:24px" align=justify>The Company accounts for uncertain tax positions using a &#147;more-likely-than-not&#148; threshold for recognizing and resolving uncertain tax positions. &nbsp;The evaluation of uncertain tax positions is based on factors including, but not limited to, changes in tax law, the measurement of tax positions taken or expected to be taken in tax returns, the effective settlement of matters subject to audit, new audit activity and changes in facts or circumstances related to a tax position. &nbsp;The Company evaluates this tax position on a quarterly basis. &nbsp;The Company also accrues for potential interest and penalties, if applicable, related to unrecognized tax benefits in income tax expense. &nbsp;(See Note G).</p> <p style="MARGIN-BOTTOM:6px; MARGIN-TOP:6px; TEXT-INDENT:24px" align=justify><i>Investment in CorNova</i></p> <p style="MARGIN-BOTTOM:6px; MARGIN-TOP:6px; TEXT-INDENT:24px" align=justify>The Company&#146;s investment in CorNova is accounted for using the cost method of accounting. &nbsp;(See Note P).</p> <p style="MARGIN-BOTTOM:6px; PADDING-LEFT:24px; MARGIN-TOP:6px" align=justify><i>Impairment of Long-Lived Assets</i></p> <p style="MARGIN-BOTTOM:6px; MARGIN-TOP:6px; TEXT-INDENT:24px" align=justify>The Company evaluates its long-lived assets, which include property and equipment, for impairment as events and circumstances indicate that the carrying amount may not be recoverable. &nbsp;The Company evaluates the realizability of its long-lived assets based on reviews of results of sales of similar assets and independent appraisals. &nbsp;As a result of the continued operating losses described above, the Company evaluated the recoverability of its property and equipment as of March 31, 2013 and 2012 and determined that during the fiscal year ended March 31, 2012, there existed an impairment of a single group of production equipment, accordingly, the Company recorded an impairment charge of $16,000 for the fiscal year ended March 31, 2012. &nbsp;The Company determined that during the fiscal year ended March 31, 2013, there existed no additional impairment of its long-lived assets.<a name=OLE_LINK5><a name=OLE_LINK6></p> <p style=MARGIN:6px align=justify><br><br></p> <p style="MARGIN-BOTTOM:0px; MARGIN-TOP:26px" align=center>F-11</p> <p style=MARGIN:0px><br></p> <hr size=1 noshade style="MARGIN-BOTTOM:9px; PADDING-TOP:9px"> <p style="MARGIN-BOTTOM:6px; PAGE-BREAK-BEFORE:always; MARGIN-TOP:0px" align=center><b>ADVANSOURCE BIOMATERIALS CORPORATION</b></p> <p style="MARGIN-BOTTOM:6px; MARGIN-TOP:0px" align=center><b>NOTES TO CONSOLIDATED FINANCIAL STATEMENTS</b></p> <p style=MARGIN:0px><br></p> <p style="MARGIN-BOTTOM:6px; PADDING-LEFT:24px; MARGIN-TOP:6px" align=justify><i>Stock-Based Compensation</i></p> <p style="MARGIN-BOTTOM:6px; MARGIN-TOP:0px; TEXT-INDENT:24px" align=justify>Stock-based compensation is measured at the grant date based on the estimated fair value of the award and is recognized as an expense over the requisite service period. &nbsp;The valuation of employee stock options is an inherently subjective process, since market values are generally not available for long-term, non-transferable employee stock options. &nbsp;Accordingly, the Black-Scholes option pricing model is utilized to derive an estimated fair value. &nbsp;The Black-Scholes pricing model requires the consideration of the following six variables for purposes of estimating fair value:</p> <p style="MARGIN-BOTTOM:-2px; FONT-FAMILY:Symbol; FLOAT:left; MARGIN-TOP:0px; WIDTH:72px; TEXT-INDENT:48px">&#183;</p> <p style="MARGIN-BOTTOM:6px; PADDING-LEFT:72px; MARGIN-TOP:0px; TEXT-INDENT:-2px" align=justify>the stock option exercise price;</p> <p style="MARGIN-BOTTOM:-2px; FONT-FAMILY:Symbol; FLOAT:left; CLEAR:left; MARGIN-TOP:0px; WIDTH:72px; TEXT-INDENT:48px">&#183;</p> <p style="MARGIN-BOTTOM:6px; PADDING-LEFT:72px; MARGIN-TOP:0px; TEXT-INDENT:-2px" align=justify>the expected term of the option;</p> <p style="MARGIN-BOTTOM:-2px; FONT-FAMILY:Symbol; FLOAT:left; CLEAR:left; MARGIN-TOP:0px; WIDTH:72px; TEXT-INDENT:48px">&#183;</p> <p style="MARGIN-BOTTOM:6px; PADDING-LEFT:72px; MARGIN-TOP:0px; TEXT-INDENT:-2px" align=justify>the grant date price of the Company&#146;s common stock, which is issuable upon exercise of the option;</p> <p style="MARGIN-BOTTOM:-2px; FONT-FAMILY:Symbol; FLOAT:left; CLEAR:left; MARGIN-TOP:0px; WIDTH:72px; TEXT-INDENT:48px">&#183;</p> <p style="MARGIN-BOTTOM:6px; PADDING-LEFT:72px; MARGIN-TOP:0px; TEXT-INDENT:-2px" align=justify>the expected volatility of the Company&#146;s common stock;</p> <p style="MARGIN-BOTTOM:-2px; FONT-FAMILY:Symbol; FLOAT:left; CLEAR:left; MARGIN-TOP:0px; WIDTH:72px; TEXT-INDENT:48px">&#183;</p> <p style="MARGIN-BOTTOM:6px; PADDING-LEFT:72px; MARGIN-TOP:0px; TEXT-INDENT:-2px" align=justify>the expected dividends on the Company&#146;s common stock (the Company does not anticipate paying dividends in the foreseeable future); and</p> <p style="MARGIN-BOTTOM:-2px; FONT-FAMILY:Symbol; FLOAT:left; CLEAR:left; MARGIN-TOP:0px; WIDTH:72px; TEXT-INDENT:48px">&#183;</p> <p style="MARGIN-BOTTOM:6px; PADDING-LEFT:72px; MARGIN-TOP:0px; TEXT-INDENT:-2px" align=justify>the risk free interest rate for the expected option term.</p> <p style="MARGIN-BOTTOM:6px; CLEAR:left; MARGIN-TOP:0px; TEXT-INDENT:24px">There were no options granted during the fiscal years ended March 31, 2013 and 2012.</p> <p style="MARGIN-BOTTOM:6px; MARGIN-TOP:0px; TEXT-INDENT:24px" align=justify><u>Expected Dividends.</u> &nbsp;The Company has never declared or paid any cash dividends on any of its capital stock and does not expect to do so in the foreseeable future. &nbsp;Accordingly, the Company uses an expected dividend yield of zero to calculate the grant-date fair value of a stock option.</p> <p style="MARGIN-BOTTOM:6px; MARGIN-TOP:0px; TEXT-INDENT:24px" align=justify><u>Expected Volatility.</u> &nbsp;The expected volatility is a measure of the amount by which the Company&#146;s stock price is expected to fluctuate during the expected term of options granted. &nbsp;The Company determines the expected volatility solely based upon the historical volatility of its common stock over a period commensurate with the option&#146;s expected term. &nbsp;The Company does not believe that the future volatility of its common stock over an option&#146;s expected term is likely to differ significantly from the past.</p> <p style="MARGIN-BOTTOM:6px; MARGIN-TOP:0px; TEXT-INDENT:24px" align=justify><u>Risk-Free Interest Rate.</u> &nbsp;The risk-free interest rate is the implied yield available on U.S. Treasury zero-coupon issues with a remaining term equal to the option&#146;s expected term on the grant date.</p> <p style="MARGIN-BOTTOM:6px; MARGIN-TOP:0px; TEXT-INDENT:24px" align=justify><u>Expected Term.</u> &nbsp;For option grants subsequent to the adoption of the fair value recognition provisions of the accounting standards, the expected life of stock options granted is based on the actual vesting date and the end of the contractual term.</p> <p style="MARGIN-BOTTOM:6px; MARGIN-TOP:0px; TEXT-INDENT:24px" align=justify><u>Stock Option Exercise Price and Grant Date Price of Common Stock.</u> &nbsp;The closing market price of the Company&#146;s common stock on the date of grant.</p> <p style="MARGIN-BOTTOM:6px; MARGIN-TOP:0px; TEXT-INDENT:24px" align=justify>The Company is required to estimate the level of award forfeitures expected to occur and record compensation expense only for those awards that are ultimately expected to vest. &nbsp;This requirement applies to all awards that are not yet vested. &nbsp;Due to the limited number of unvested options outstanding, the majority of which are held by executives and members of the Company&#146;s Board of Directors, the Company has estimated a zero forfeiture rate. &nbsp;The Company will revisit this assumption periodically and as changes in the composition of the option pool dictate. </p> <p style="MARGIN-BOTTOM:6px; MARGIN-TOP:0px" align=justify><br><br></p> <p style="MARGIN-BOTTOM:0px; MARGIN-TOP:26px" align=center>F-12</p> <p style=MARGIN:0px><br></p> <hr size=1 noshade style="MARGIN-BOTTOM:9px; PADDING-TOP:9px"> <p style="MARGIN-BOTTOM:6px; PAGE-BREAK-BEFORE:always; MARGIN-TOP:0px" align=center><b>ADVANSOURCE BIOMATERIALS CORPORATION</b></p> <p style="MARGIN-BOTTOM:6px; MARGIN-TOP:0px" align=center><b>NOTES TO CONSOLIDATED FINANCIAL STATEMENTS</b></p> <p style=MARGIN:0px><br></p> <p style="MARGIN-BOTTOM:6px; PADDING-LEFT:24px; MARGIN-TOP:0px" align=justify><i>Fair Value of Financial Instruments</i></p> <p style="MARGIN-BOTTOM:6px; MARGIN-TOP:0px; TEXT-INDENT:24px" align=justify>The Company follows Accounting Standards Codification 820-10 (&#147;ASC 820-10&#148;), <i>&#147;Fair Value Measurements and Disclosures,&#148;</i> for fair value measurements. &nbsp;ASC 820-10 defines fair value, establishes a framework for measuring fair value, and expands disclosures about fair value measurements. &nbsp;The standard provides a consistent definition of fair value, which focuses on an exit price, which is the price that would be received to sell an asset or paid to transfer a liability in an orderly transaction between market participants at the measurement date. &nbsp;The standard also prioritizes, within the measurement of fair value, the use of market-based information over entity specific information and establishes a three-level hierarchy for fair value measurement based on the nature of inputs used in the valuation of an asset or liability as of the measurement date.</p> <p style="MARGIN-BOTTOM:6px; MARGIN-TOP:0px; TEXT-INDENT:24px" align=justify>The hierarchy established under ASC 820-10 gives the highest priority to unadjusted quoted prices in active markets for identical assets or liabilities (Level 1) and the lowest priority to unobservable inputs (Level 3). &nbsp;The three levels of the fair value hierarchy under ASC 820-10 are described below:</p> <p style="MARGIN-BOTTOM:6px; MARGIN-TOP:0px; TEXT-INDENT:24px" align=justify>Level 1 &#150; Pricing inputs are quoted prices available in active markets for identical investments as of the reporting date. &nbsp;As required by ASC 820-10, the Company does not adjust the quoted price for these investments, even in situations where the Company holds a large position and a sale could reasonably impact the quoted price.</p> <p style="MARGIN-BOTTOM:6px; MARGIN-TOP:0px; TEXT-INDENT:24px" align=justify>Level 2 &#150; Pricing inputs are quoted prices for similar investments, or inputs that are observable, either directly or indirectly, for substantially the full term through corroboration with observable market data. &nbsp;Level 2 includes investments valued at quoted prices adjusted for legal or contractual restrictions specific to these investments.</p> <p style="MARGIN-BOTTOM:6px; MARGIN-TOP:0px; TEXT-INDENT:24px" align=justify>Level 3 &#150; Pricing inputs are unobservable for the investment, that is, inputs that reflect the reporting entity&#146;s own assumptions about the assumptions market participants would use in pricing the asset or liability. &nbsp;Level 3 includes investments that are supported by little or no market activity.</p> <p style="MARGIN-BOTTOM:6px; MARGIN-TOP:6px; TEXT-INDENT:24px" align=justify>In January 2010, the Financial Accounting Standards Board issued Accounting Standards Update 2010-06 (&#147;ASU 2010-06&#148;), &#147;Improving Disclosures About Fair Value Measurements,&#148; which requires interim disclosures regarding significant transfers in and out of Level 1 and Level 2 fair value measurements. &nbsp;Additionally, ASU 2010-06 requires disclosure for each class of assets and liabilities and disclosures about the valuation techniques and inputs used to measure fair value for both recurring and non-recurring fair value measurements. &nbsp;These disclosures are required for fair value measurements that fall in either Level 2 or Level 3. &nbsp;Further, ASU 2010-06 requires separate presentation of Level 3 activity for the fair value measurements. &nbsp;The Company adopted the provisions of this standard on April 1, 2010.</p> <p style="MARGIN-BOTTOM:6px; MARGIN-TOP:6px; TEXT-INDENT:24px" align=justify>The following table summarizes the Company&#146;s assets measured at fair value on a nonrecurring basis in the Company&#146;s balance sheet at March 31, 2012:</p> <table bordercolor=transparent style="FONT-SIZE:10pt; MARGIN-TOP:0px; TEXT-INDENT:24px" align=justify>As a result of the Company&#146;s evaluation of the recoverability of its property, plant and equipment, the Company recorded impairment of a single group of production equipment that existed during the fiscal year ended March 31, 2012, accordingly, the Company recorded an impairment charge of $16,000. &nbsp;The Company determined that during the fiscal year ended March 31, 2013, there existed no additional impairment of its long-lived assets.</p> <p style="MARGIN-BOTTOM:6px; MARGIN-TOP:0px" align=justify><br><br></p> <p style="MARGIN-BOTTOM:0px; MARGIN-TOP:26px" align=center>F-14</p> <p style=MARGIN:0px><br></p> <hr size=1 noshade style="MARGIN-BOTTOM:9px; PADDING-TOP:9px"> <p style="MARGIN-BOTTOM:6px; PAGE-BREAK-BEFORE:always; MARGIN-TOP:0px" align=center><b>ADVANSOURCE BIOMATERIALS CORPORATION</b></p> <p style="MARGIN-BOTTOM:6px; MARGIN-TOP:0px" align=center><b>NOTES TO CONSOLIDATED FINANCIAL STATEMENTS</b></p> <p style=MARGIN:0px><br></p> <p style="MARGIN-BOTTOM:6px; MARGIN-TOP:0px; TEXT-INDENT:24px" align=justify>On December 22, 2011, we entered into an agreement with an independent third-party under which we sold and leased back our land and building generating gross proceeds of $2,000,000. &nbsp;The initial minimum lease term is 15 years. &nbsp;At the end of the initial minimum lease term, we have the option to renew the lease for three periods of five years each. &nbsp;Under the terms of the lease, we have provided, as collateral, a security interest in all furnishings, fixtures and equipment owned and used by us, having a net book value of approximately $95,000 as of March 31, 2013. &nbsp;For accounting purposes, the provision of such collateral constitutes continuing involvement with the associated property. &nbsp;Due to this continuing involvement, this sale-leaseback transaction is accounted for under the financing method, rather than as a completed sale. &nbsp;Under the financing method, we include the sales proceeds received as a financing obligation. &nbsp;The building, building improvements and land remain on the consolidated balance sheet and the building and building improvements will continue to be depreciated over their remaining useful lives. &nbsp;Payments made under the lease are applied as payments of imputed interest and deemed principal on the underlying financing obligation.</p> <p style="MARGIN-BOTTOM:-1pt; FONT-SIZE:1pt; MARGIN-TOP:6px" /> <p style="MARGIN-BOTTOM:-2px; FLOAT:left; MARGIN-TOP:0px; WIDTH:48px; TEXT-INDENT:24px"><b>G.</b></p> <p style="MARGIN-BOTTOM:6px; PADDING-LEFT:48px; MARGIN-TOP:0px; TEXT-INDENT:-2px" align=justify><b>Income Taxes</b></p><a name=E_IncomeTaxes_025252> <p style="MARGIN-BOTTOM:6px; CLEAR:left; MARGIN-TOP:6px; TEXT-INDENT:24px" align=justify>As of March 31, 2013 and 2012, the Company had no material unrecognized tax benefits and no adjustments to liabilities or operations were required.</p> <p style="MARGIN-BOTTOM:6px; MARGIN-TOP:6px; TEXT-INDENT:24px" align=justify>The Company may, from time to time, be assessed interest or penalties by major tax jurisdictions. &nbsp;The Company recognizes interest and penalties related to uncertain tax positions in income tax expense. &nbsp;No interest and penalties have been recognized by the Company to date.</p> <p style="MARGIN-BOTTOM:6px; MARGIN-TOP:6px; TEXT-INDENT:24px" align=justify>Tax years 2009 through 2013 are subject to examination by the federal and state taxing authorities. &nbsp;There are no income tax examinations currently in process.</p> <p style="MARGIN-BOTTOM:6px; MARGIN-TOP:0px" align=justify><br><br></p> <p style="MARGIN-BOTTOM:0px; MARGIN-TOP:26px" align=center>F-16</p> <p style=MARGIN:0px><br></p> <hr size=1 noshade style="MARGIN-BOTTOM:9px; PADDING-TOP:9px"> <p style="MARGIN-BOTTOM:6px; PAGE-BREAK-BEFORE:always; MARGIN-TOP:0px" align=center><b>ADVANSOURCE BIOMATERIALS CORPORATION</b></p> <p style="MARGIN-BOTTOM:6px; MARGIN-TOP:0px" align=center><b>NOTES TO CONSOLIDATED FINANCIAL STATEMENTS</b></p> <p style=MARGIN:0px><br></p> <p style="MARGIN-BOTTOM:-2px; FLOAT:left; MARGIN-TOP:0px; WIDTH:48px; TEXT-INDENT:24px"><b>H.</b></p> <p style="MARGIN-BOTTOM:6px; PADDING-LEFT:48px; MARGIN-TOP:0px; TEXT-INDENT:-2px" align=justify><b>Promissory Note</b></p> <p style="MARGIN-BOTTOM:6px; CLEAR:left; MARGIN-TOP:6px; TEXT-INDENT:24px" align=justify>On July 7, 2011, the Company entered into a Commercial Real Estate Promissory Note in the principal amount of $800,000 (the &#147;Note&#148;) with Axiom Partners, LP as the lender (the &#147;Lender&#148;). &nbsp;The Note had a two-year term and interest at the rate of 15% per annum. &nbsp;The Note provided for monthly interest payments to be paid on the last calendar day of each month commencing on August 31, 2011. &nbsp;A balloon payment of the principal balance of $800,000, plus any accrued and unpaid interest, was due upon the maturity of the Note on July 8, 2013. &nbsp;The Note was secured by the Company&#146;s land and building pursuant to the terms and conditions of the Note and a mortgage in favor of the Lender (the &#147;Mortgage&#148;). &nbsp;The Note contained a penalty provision equal to $166,000, less the amount of interest actually paid to the Lender, in the event of an early prepayment. &nbsp;During the fiscal year ended March 31, 2012, the Company paid approximately $56,000 of interest incurred on the Note.</p> <p style="MARGIN-BOTTOM:6px; MARGIN-TOP:6px; TEXT-INDENT:24px" align=justify>In connection with this transaction, the Company also incurred approximately $68,000 in fees, primarily for legal and placement activities, which were recorded as deferred financing costs in the consolidated balance sheet. &nbsp;Deferred financing costs were to be amortized over the 24-month term of the Note using the effective interest rate method. &nbsp;During the fiscal year ended March 31, 2012, the Company amortized approximately $16,000 of these costs, which are reported as additional interest expense in the consolidated statement of operations.</p> <p style="MARGIN-BOTTOM:6px; MARGIN-TOP:6px; TEXT-INDENT:24px" align=justify>On December 22, 2011, in connection with the sale of the Company&#146;s land and building, the Note was paid in full, including a prepayment penalty of approximately $99,000, as provided for in the Note and amended by the Lender at the time of the sale of the Company&#146;s land and building, and the mortgage was discharged (See Note I). &nbsp;The prepayment penalty and the write-off of the remaining unamortized deferred financing costs of $52,000 are included in the loss on the extinguishment of promissory note for the fiscal year ended March 31, 2012 in the consolidated statement of operations.</p> <p style="MARGIN-BOTTOM:-2px; FLOAT:left; MARGIN-TOP:0px; WIDTH:48px; TEXT-INDENT:24px"><b>I.</b></p> <p style="MARGIN-BOTTOM:6px; PADDING-LEFT:48px; MARGIN-TOP:0px; TEXT-INDENT:-2px" align=justify><b>Long-Term Financing Obligation</b></p> <p style="MARGIN-BOTTOM:6px; CLEAR:left; MARGIN-TOP:0px; TEXT-INDENT:24px" align=justify>On December 22, 2011, the Company entered into an agreement with an independent third-party under which we sold and leased back our land and building generating gross proceeds of $2,000,000. &nbsp;Pursuant to a lease agreement, the initial minimum lease term is 15 years. &nbsp;At the end of the initial minimum lease term, we have the option to renew the lease for three periods of five years each. &nbsp;Under the terms of the lease, we were required to place $280,000 of the net proceeds in escrow as a prepayment of the calendar year 2012 lease payments. &nbsp;As of March 31, 2012, the balance of the prepaid lease payment was $210,000 and is included in prepaid expenses and other current assets of the consolidated balance sheets. &nbsp;In addition, we provided, as collateral, a security interest in all furnishings, fixtures and equipment owned and used by us, having a net book value of approximately $146,000 as of March 31, 2012. &nbsp;For accounting purposes, the provision of such collateral constitutes continuing involvement with the associated property. &nbsp;Due to this continuing involvement, this sale-leaseback transaction is accounted for under the financing method, rather than as a completed sale. &nbsp;Under the financing method, we include the sales proceeds received as a financing obligation. &nbsp;As of March 31, 2013 and 2012, the total financing obligation was $1,986,000, respectively. &nbsp;The building, building improvements and land remain on the consolidated balance sheet and the building and building improvements will continue to be depreciated over their remaining useful lives. &nbsp;Payments made under the lease are applied as payments of imputed interest and deemed principal on the underlying financing obligation.</p> <p style="MARGIN-BOTTOM:6px; MARGIN-TOP:0px" align=justify><br><br></p> <p style="MARGIN-BOTTOM:0px; MARGIN-TOP:26px" align=center>F-17</p> <p style=MARGIN:0px><br></p> <hr size=1 noshade style="MARGIN-BOTTOM:9px; PADDING-TOP:9px"> <p style="MARGIN-BOTTOM:6px; FLOAT:left; MARGIN-TOP:0px; WIDTH:48px; TEXT-INDENT:24px"><b>J.</b></p> <p style="MARGIN-BOTTOM:6px; PADDING-LEFT:48px; MARGIN-TOP:0px; TEXT-INDENT:-2px" align=justify><b>Contingencies</b></p> <p style="MARGIN-BOTTOM:6px; CLEAR:left; MARGIN-TOP:0px; TEXT-INDENT:24px" align=justify>The Company is not a party to any legal proceedings, other than ordinary routine litigation incidental to its business, which the Company believes will not have a material affect on its financial position or results of operations.</p> <p style="MARGIN-BOTTOM:-2px; FLOAT:left; MARGIN-TOP:0px; WIDTH:48px; TEXT-INDENT:24px"><b>K.</b></p> <p style="MARGIN-BOTTOM:6px; PADDING-LEFT:48px; MARGIN-TOP:0px; TEXT-INDENT:-2px" align=justify><b>Concentration of Credit Risk and Major Customers</b></p> <p style="MARGIN-BOTTOM:6px; CLEAR:left; MARGIN-TOP:6px; TEXT-INDENT:24px" align=justify>For the year ended March 31, 2013, three customers represented 33%, 17% and 13% of revenues, respectively. &nbsp;For the year ended March 31, 2012, two customers represented 30% and 24%, respectively, of our revenues.</p> <p style="MARGIN-BOTTOM:6px; MARGIN-TOP:6px; TEXT-INDENT:24px" align=justify>As of March 31, 2013, the Company had accounts receivable-trade of $95,000, or 65%, due from three customers. &nbsp;As of March 31, 2012, the Company had accounts receivable-trade of $145,000, or 97%, due from three customers.</p> <p style="MARGIN-BOTTOM:6px; MARGIN-TOP:6px; TEXT-INDENT:24px" align=justify>As of March 31, 2013, the Company had $208,000 due from two customers related to receivables on license fees and royalties. &nbsp;As of March 31, 2012, the Company had $142,000 due from four customers related to receivables on license fees and royalties. &nbsp;These amounts are classified as accounts receivable-other in the Company&#146;s consolidated balance sheets.</p> <p style="MARGIN-BOTTOM:6px; MARGIN-TOP:6px; TEXT-INDENT:24px" align=justify>During the year ended March 31, 2013, four vendors represented, in the aggregate, $93,000, or 81%, of material purchases used in the production process. &nbsp;During the year ended March 31, 2012, four vendors represented, in the aggregate, $101,000, or 76%, of material purchases used in the production process.</p><a name=H_RevolvingLineOfCredit_025813><a name=I_StockholdersEquity_025817> <p style=MARGIN:6px align=justify><br><br></p> <p style="MARGIN-BOTTOM:0px; MARGIN-TOP:26px" align=center>F-18</p> <p style=MARGIN:0px><br></p> <hr size=1 noshade style="MARGIN-BOTTOM:9px; PADDING-TOP:9px"> <p style="MARGIN-BOTTOM:6px; PAGE-BREAK-BEFORE:always; MARGIN-TOP:0px" align=center><b>ADVANSOURCE BIOMATERIALS CORPORATION</b></p> <p style="MARGIN-BOTTOM:6px; MARGIN-TOP:0px" align=center><b>NOTES TO CONSOLIDATED FINANCIAL STATEMENTS</b></p> <p style=MARGIN:0px><br></p> <p style="MARGIN-BOTTOM:-1pt; FONT-SIZE:1pt; MARGIN-TOP:6px" /> <p style="MARGIN-BOTTOM:-2px; FLOAT:left; MARGIN-TOP:0px; WIDTH:48px; TEXT-INDENT:24px"><b>L.</b></p> <p style="MARGIN-BOTTOM:6px; PADDING-LEFT:48px; MARGIN-TOP:0px; TEXT-INDENT:-2px" align=justify><b>Stockholders&#146; Equity</b></p> <p style="MARGIN-BOTTOM:6px; CLEAR:left; MARGIN-TOP:6px; TEXT-INDENT:24px" align=justify><i>Preferred Stock</i></p> <p style="MARGIN-BOTTOM:6px; MARGIN-TOP:6px; TEXT-INDENT:24px" align=justify>The Company has authorized 5,000,000 shares, $0.001 par value, Preferred Stock (the Preferred Stock&#148;) of which 500,000 shares have been issued and redeemed, therefore are not considered outstanding. &nbsp;In addition, 500,000 shares of Preferred Stock have been designated as Series A Junior Participating Preferred Stock (the &#147;Junior Preferred Stock&#148;) with the designations and the powers, preferences and rights, and the qualifications, limitations and restrictions specified in the Certificate of Designation of the Junior Preferred Stock filed with the Delaware Department of State on January 28, 2008. &nbsp;Such number of shares may be increased or decreased by resolution of the Board of Directors; provided, that no decrease shall reduce the number of shares of Junior Preferred Stock to a number less than the number of shares then outstanding plus the number of shares reserved for issuance upon the exercise of outstanding options, rights or warrants or upon the conversion of any outstanding securities issued by the Company convertible into Junior Preferred Stock. &nbsp;As of March 31, 2013, there was no Junior Preferred Stock issued or outstanding.</p> <p style="MARGIN-BOTTOM:6px; MARGIN-TOP:0px; TEXT-INDENT:24px" align=justify><i>Common Stock Options and Warrants</i></p> <p style="MARGIN-BOTTOM:6px; MARGIN-TOP:0px; TEXT-INDENT:24px" align=justify>On March 31, 2008, the Company issued warrants to the investment bankers, who assisted in the sale of a former subsidiary, to purchase 219,298 shares of common stock at an exercise price of $0.874 per share, which are exercisable until March 31, 2015. &nbsp;The warrants were valued at $76,000 using the Black-Scholes model and treated as permanent equity.</p> <p style="MARGIN-BOTTOM:6px; MARGIN-TOP:0px; TEXT-INDENT:24px" align=justify>There were no exercises of options or warrants by employees and consultants during the fiscal years ended March 31, 2013 and 2012.</p> <p style="MARGIN-BOTTOM:6px; MARGIN-TOP:0px; TEXT-INDENT:24px" align=justify><i>Employee Stock Purchase Plan</i></p> <p style="MARGIN-BOTTOM:6px; MARGIN-TOP:0px; TEXT-INDENT:24px" align=justify>During the fiscal year ended March 31, 2012, the Company issued 140,566 shares of its common stock to its employees pursuant to the terms of the Employee Stock Purchase Plan (the &#147;ESP Plan&#148;), as amended, and received cash proceeds of approximately $7,000. &nbsp;During the fiscal year ended March 31, 2012, the Company also recorded stock compensation of $1,000 to reflect the effect of the benefit received by the employees for the issuance of common stock at a 15% discount to the fair market value of the Company&#146;s common stock on the settlement date. &nbsp;As of March 31, 2012, the Company issued all 500,000 shares authorized for issuance under the ESP Plan. &nbsp;Accordingly, there were no shares of its common stock available for issuance or issued pursuant to the ESP Plan during the fiscal year ended March 31, 2013.</p> <p style="MARGIN-BOTTOM:6px; MARGIN-TOP:0px; TEXT-INDENT:24px" align=justify><i>Treasury Stock and Other Transactions</i></p> <p style="MARGIN-BOTTOM:6px; MARGIN-TOP:0px; TEXT-INDENT:24px" align=justify>In June 2001, the Board of Directors adopted a share repurchase program authorizing the repurchase by the Company of up to 250,000 of its shares of common stock. &nbsp;In June 2004, the Board of Directors authorized the purchase of an additional 500,000 shares of common stock. &nbsp;Since June 2001, a total of 251,379 shares have been repurchased by the Company under the share repurchase program, leaving 498,621 shares remaining to purchase under the share repurchase program. &nbsp;No repurchases were made during the years ended March 31, 2013 and 2012. &nbsp;The share repurchase program authorizes repurchases from time to time in open market transactions, through privately negotiated transactions, block transactions or otherwise, at times and prices deemed appropriate by management, and is not subject to an expiration date.</p> <p style="MARGIN-BOTTOM:6px; MARGIN-TOP:0px" align=justify><br><br></p> <p style="MARGIN-BOTTOM:0px; MARGIN-TOP:26px" align=center>F-19</p> <p style=MARGIN:0px><br></p> <hr size=1 noshade style="MARGIN-BOTTOM:9px; PADDING-TOP:9px"> <p style="MARGIN-BOTTOM:6px; PAGE-BREAK-BEFORE:always; MARGIN-TOP:0px" align=center><b>ADVANSOURCE BIOMATERIALS CORPORATION</b></p> <p style="MARGIN-BOTTOM:6px; MARGIN-TOP:0px" align=center><b>NOTES TO CONSOLIDATED FINANCIAL STATEMENTS</b></p> <p style=MARGIN:0px><br></p> <p style="MARGIN-BOTTOM:6px; MARGIN-TOP:0px; TEXT-INDENT:24px" align=justify><i>Stockholder Rights Plan</i></p> <p style="MARGIN-BOTTOM:6px; MARGIN-TOP:0px; TEXT-INDENT:24px" align=justify>The Company&#146;s Board of Directors approved the adoption of a stockholder rights plan (the &#147;Rights Plan&#148;) under which all stockholders of record as of February 8, 2008 will receive rights to purchase shares of the Junior Preferred Stock (the &#147;Rights&#148;). &nbsp;The Rights will be distributed as a dividend. &nbsp;Initially, the Rights will attach to, and trade with, the Company&#146;s common stock. &nbsp;Subject to the terms, conditions and limitations of the Rights Plan, the Rights will become exercisable if (among other things) a person or group acquires 15% or more of the Company&#146;s common stock. &nbsp;Upon such an event, and payment of the purchase price, each Right (except those held by the acquiring person or group) will entitle the holder to acquire shares of the Company&#146;s common stock (or the economic equivalent thereof) having a value equal to twice the purchase price. &nbsp;The Company&#146;s Board of Directors may redeem the Rights prior to the time they are triggered. &nbsp;In the event of an unsolicited attempt to acquire the Company, the Rights Plan is intended to facilitate the full realization of stockholder value in the Company and the fair and equal treatment of all Company stockholders. &nbsp;The Rights Plan does not prevent a takeover attempt.</p> <p style="MARGIN-BOTTOM:-2px; FLOAT:left; MARGIN-TOP:0px; WIDTH:48px; TEXT-INDENT:24px"><b>M.</b></p> <p style="MARGIN-BOTTOM:6px; PADDING-LEFT:48px; MARGIN-TOP:0px; TEXT-INDENT:-2px" align=justify><b>Stock Based Compensation</b></p><a name=J_EnterpriseAndRelatedGeographicI_030715><a name=K_SupplementalDisclosuresForStock_030909> <p style="MARGIN-BOTTOM:6px; CLEAR:left; MARGIN-TOP:0px; TEXT-INDENT:24px" align=justify>AdvanSource&#146;s 1996 Employee, Director and Consultants Stock Option Plan (the &#147;1996 Plan&#148;) was approved by AdvanSource&#146;s Board of Directors and Stockholders in March 1996. &nbsp;A total of 7,000,000 shares have been reserved for issuance under the Plan. &nbsp;Under the terms of the Plan, the exercise price of Incentive Stock Options issued under the Plan must be equal to the fair market value of the common stock at the date of grant. &nbsp;In the event that Non Qualified Options are granted under the Plan, the exercise price may be less than the fair market value of the common stock at the time of the grant (but not less than par value). &nbsp;In October 2003, the Company&#146;s shareholders approved the AdvanSource 2003 Stock Option Plan (the &#147;2003 Plan&#148;), which authorizes the issuance of 3,000,000 shares of common stock with terms similar to the 1996 Plan. &nbsp;In January 2006, the Company filed Form S-8 with the Securities and Exchange Commission registering an additional 489,920 total shares of common stock in the 1996 Plan and 2003 Plan. &nbsp;Total shares of common stock registered under the 1996 Plan and 2003 Plan (collectively, the &#147;Plans&#148;) are 10,489,920. &nbsp;Substantially all of the stock options granted pursuant to the 1996 Plan provide for the acceleration of vesting of the shares of Common Stock subject to such options in connection with certain changes in control of the Company. &nbsp;A similar provision is not included in the 2003 Plan. &nbsp;In February 2008, the Company filed two Forms S-8 to register 360,000 shares of common stock in connection with previously granted stock options to two executives who received grants of unregistered shares under Rule 711 of NYSE Amex. &nbsp;Normally, options granted expire ten years from the grant date.</p> <p style="MARGIN-BOTTOM:6px; PAGE-BREAK-BEFORE:always; MARGIN-TOP:0px" align=center><b>ADVANSOURCE BIOMATERIALS CORPORATION</b></p> <p style="MARGIN-BOTTOM:6px; MARGIN-TOP:0px" align=center><b>NOTES TO CONSOLIDATED FINANCIAL STATEMENTS</b></p> <p style=MARGIN:0px><br></p> <p style="MARGIN-BOTTOM:6px; MARGIN-TOP:0px; TEXT-INDENT:24px" align=justify>At March 31, 2013, there were no shares remaining to be granted under the 1996 Stock Option Plan and 771,250 shares were available for grant under the 2003 Stock Option Plan.</p> <p style="MARGIN-BOTTOM:6px; MARGIN-TOP:0px; TEXT-INDENT:24px" align=justify>For the fiscal years ended March 31, 2013 and 2012, the Company recorded stock-based compensation expense for options of approximately $33,000 and $44,000, respectively. &nbsp;As of March 31, 2013, the Company has approximately $8,000 of unrecognized compensation cost related to stock options that is expected to be recognized as expense over a weighted-average period of .39 years.<a name=OLE_LINK1><a name=OLE_LINK2></p><a name=M_OtherAgreements_033203><a name=N_ValuationAndQualifyingAccounts_033319><a name=O_BenefitPlanAndEmploymentAgreeme_033551> <p style="MARGIN-BOTTOM:-2px; FLOAT:left; MARGIN-TOP:0px; WIDTH:48px; TEXT-INDENT:24px"><b>N.</b></p> <p style="MARGIN-BOTTOM:6px; PADDING-LEFT:48px; MARGIN-TOP:0px; TEXT-INDENT:-2px" align=justify><b>Benefit Plans and Employment Agreements of Executive Officers</b></p> <p style="MARGIN-BOTTOM:6px; CLEAR:left; MARGIN-TOP:0px; TEXT-INDENT:24px" align=justify>The Company has the AdvanSource 401(k) Retirement Savings Plan established under Section 401(k) of the Internal Revenue Code. &nbsp;All full-time employees who are twenty-one years of age are eligible to participate on the beginning of the first month after 30 days of employment. &nbsp;The Company&#146;s contributions are discretionary. &nbsp;The Company made matching contributions of approximately $9,000 and $8,000 during the fiscal years ended March 31, 2013 and 2012, respectively.</p> <p style="MARGIN-BOTTOM:6px; MARGIN-TOP:0px; TEXT-INDENT:24px" align=justify>On August 7, 2006, the Company appointed Michael F. Adams as Chief Executive Officer and President of the Company. &nbsp;Mr. Adams has been a director of the Company since May 1999 and joined the Company as its Vice President of Regulatory Affairs and Business Development on April 1, 2006. &nbsp;The Company entered into an employment agreement with Mr. Adams (the &#147;Adams Agreement&#148;) on September 13, 2006. &nbsp;Under the terms of the Adams Agreement, Mr. Adams will be employed by the Company for two years and receive an annual base salary of $290,000, as amended, which is subject to annual review by the Company&#146;s Board of Directors. &nbsp;During the Employment Period, as defined in the Adams Agreement, Mr. Adams may receive an annual bonus to be determined at the sole discretion of the Compensation Committee of the Board of Directors. &nbsp;The Company did not renew the Adams Agreement at the end of the initial term, however, the Adams agreement provides that lacking any express agreement between the parties at the end of the Employment Period, the Adams Agreement shall be deemed to continue on a month-to-month basis. &nbsp;As a result, the Adams Agreement currently continues on a month-to-month basis and is subject to all of the terms and conditions of the Adams Agreement. &nbsp;Either party has the right to terminate the Adams Agreement upon 30 days written notice. &nbsp;Mr. Adams is eligible for participation in all executive benefit programs, including health insurance, life insurance, and stock-based compensation. &nbsp;If Mr. Adams&#146; employment is terminated without cause, the Company is obligated to (i) pay Mr. Adams an amount equal to two times his annual base salary upon such termination, (ii) provide Mr. Adams with health insurance benefits for a period of 18 months after such termination, of which the premiums for the first six months after such termination shall be paid by the Company, and (iii) provide Mr. Adams life insurance benefits for one year after such termination at the Company&#146;s expense. &nbsp;During the fiscal year ended March 31, 2010, the Compensation Committee of the Board of Directors approved an increase in Mr. Adams&#146; annual base salary to $320,000. &nbsp;There was no bonus awarded to Mr. Adams during the fiscal years ended March 31, 2013 and 2012.</p><a name=P_InvestmentInCornovainc__033617> <p style="MARGIN-BOTTOM:-2px; FLOAT:left; MARGIN-TOP:0px; WIDTH:48px; TEXT-INDENT:24px"><b>O.</b></p> <p style="MARGIN-BOTTOM:6px; PADDING-LEFT:48px; MARGIN-TOP:0px; TEXT-INDENT:-2px" align=justify><b>Investment in CorNova, Inc.</b></p> <p style="MARGIN-BOTTOM:6px; CLEAR:left; MARGIN-TOP:0px; TEXT-INDENT:24px" align=justify>The Company partnered with CorNova, Inc. (&#147;CorNova&#148;), a privately-held, development stage company, which is developing medical devices for cardiovascular applications. &nbsp;In March 2004, the Company entered into an Exchange and Venture Agreement by and among the Company, Implant Sciences Corporation and CorNova. &nbsp;During the fiscal years ended March 31, 2004 and 2005, the Company contributed, in the aggregate, 321,573 shares of its common stock, valued at approximately $825,000, which provided the Company a 30% ownership interest in the common stock of CorNova. &nbsp;The Company initially used the equity method of accounting; accordingly, it recorded 30% of the net loss of CorNova in its financial statements through the fiscal year ended March 31, 2007. &nbsp;During the fiscal year ended March 31, 2007, the Company recorded equity in the net loss of CorNova of $279,000, and equity in comprehensive income of CorNova of $40,000 (related to unrealized holding gains on securities classified as available-for-sale), which reduced the Company&#146;s investment in CorNova to $0. &nbsp;Therefore, no additional losses were recorded from the Company&#146;s equity ownership in CorNova since the fiscal year ended March 31, 2007.</p> <p style="MARGIN-BOTTOM:6px; MARGIN-TOP:0px; TEXT-INDENT:24px" align=justify>As a result of several dilutive financings by CorNova, the Company&#146;s ownership interest decreased, accordingly, the Company began using the cost method of accounting during fiscal 2009. &nbsp;As of March 31, 2013, the Company&#146;s ownership interest in CorNova was less than 1.0%.</p> <p style="MARGIN-BOTTOM:6px; MARGIN-TOP:0px" align=justify><br><br></p> <p style="MARGIN-BOTTOM:0px; MARGIN-TOP:26px" align=center>F-21</p> <p style=MARGIN:0px><br></p> <hr size=1 noshade style="MARGIN-BOTTOM:9px; PADDING-TOP:9px"> <p style="MARGIN-BOTTOM:6px; PAGE-BREAK-BEFORE:always; MARGIN-TOP:0px" align=center><b>ADVANSOURCE BIOMATERIALS CORPORATION</b></p> <p style="MARGIN-BOTTOM:6px; MARGIN-TOP:0px" align=center><b>NOTES TO CONSOLIDATED FINANCIAL STATEMENTS</b></p> <p style=MARGIN:0px><br></p> <p style="MARGIN-BOTTOM:6px; MARGIN-TOP:0px; TEXT-INDENT:24px" align=justify>The Company has no additional obligation to contribute assets or additional common stock nor to assume any liabilities or to fund any losses that CorNova may incur.<a name=Q_TerminatedAcquisitionOfCartikaM_033621></p> <p style="MARGIN-BOTTOM:-2px; FLOAT:left; MARGIN-TOP:0px; WIDTH:48px; TEXT-INDENT:24px"><b>P.</b></p> <p style="MARGIN-BOTTOM:6px; PADDING-LEFT:48px; MARGIN-TOP:0px; TEXT-INDENT:-2px" align=justify><b>Subsequent Events</b></p> <p style="MARGIN-BOTTOM:6px; CLEAR:left; MARGIN-TOP:0px; TEXT-INDENT:24px" align=justify>The Company evaluated all events or transactions that occurred after the consolidated balance sheet date through the date when the Company filed these consolidated financial statements and determined that it did not have any material recognizable subsequent events.</p> <p style="MARGIN-BOTTOM:6px; MARGIN-TOP:0px" align=justify><br><br></p> <p style="MARGIN-BOTTOM:0px; MARGIN-TOP:26px" align=center>F-22</p> <p style=MARGIN:0px><br></p> <hr size=1 noshade style="MARGIN-BOTTOM:9px; PADDING-TOP:9px"> <p style="PAGE-BREAK-BEFORE:always;
